and from this double "A prayer of Moshe, the man of Elokim," one has the power to accomplish the double "And the work of our hands establish for us, and the work of our hands, establish it," in our deeds and avodah now,

and one also has Moshe and Aharon with them—the level of Moshe (and Aharon—from the seven shepherds of Yisroel), within every Yid in Yisroel, men, women, and children,

and immediately and truly—"Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," and Moshe and Aharon with them in simplicity, souls in bodies, together with all Yidden,

and immediately and truly—"And the work of our hands, establish it" in the "Sanctuary, Hashem, which Your hands have established."

[The Rebbe gave each of those present a dollar bill, to give (or exchange) for tzedakah.]


## רשימת דברי כ"ק אדמו"ר שליט"א אור לי"ד ניסן ה'תנש"א

## 107

### Notes from the Rebbe’s Talk, Eve of 14 Nissan, 5751

**— After the sale of chametz**

A kosher and joyous Pesach, and may we draw its influence throughout the entire year. This includes, and especially so, the drawing down of all blessings in a constant manner—like the blessing of *tal* (dew), which we begin to recite on the first day of Pesach, which "cannot be stopped". May all blessings and influences be drawn down in a manner of revealed and manifest good for all of *Klal Yisrael*, in a way that "cannot be stopped."

This extends to the most essential blessing of all: the true and complete *Geulah*, a *Geulah* after which there is no exile ("cannot be stopped"). Simply put, this means that immediately and without delay we shall hear the *shofar* of *Mashiach*, and prior to that, the voice of *Eliyahu HaNavi*, may he be remembered for good, the herald of the *Geulah*, who announces that the *Geulah* has already arrived. As it is written in *Yalkut Shimoni*: "At the time when *Melech HaMashiach* comes, he stands on the roof of the *Beis HaMikdash* and calls out to *Yisrael*, saying: 'Humble ones, the time of your *Geulah* has arrived!'"

This is especially true as we stand in a special year whose acronym hints at the matter of the *Geulah*—"*Hei Tehei Shnas Ar'enu Nifla'os*" (or "*Nifla'os Ar'enu*")—that immediately and without delay the "I will show you wonders" (*Ar'enu Nifla'os*) will take place. "*Ar'enu*" specifically, meaning that we will see with physical eyes the "wonders" of the true and complete *Geulah* ("As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders"), and in a manner of "*Hei Tehei*," "it shall be in its essence," which denotes strength and eternity.

In addition to all this, there is also the virtue of this year...

## 108

...regarding the status of *chazakah* (presumption/established status)—that the beginning of the year (*Rosh Hashanah*) occurred in a "tripled" manner, three consecutive days of *Yom Tov* and *Shabbos*. Similarly, the first days of *Sukkos* and *Shemini Atzeres* and *Simchas Torah* were in a "tripled" manner—three times tripled. This is especially relevant to the festival of Pesach, which contains three primary elements: *Pesach, Matzah,* and *Maror*—so that the strength of *chazakah* is established in all the aforementioned matters.

May it be the will—and this is the main thing—that from the speech regarding all this (which relates to Pesach, as it is brought in the writings of the *AriZal* that "*Pesach*" is "*Peh Sach*"—"a mouth that speaks"), the action will be drawn down and come to fruition immediately and without delay. This includes, and especially so, regarding the offering of the *Korban Pesach* tomorrow, on *Erev Pesach*, so that there will be no need to recite the "Order of the *Korban Pesach*" in speech (as it is written, "And we will render [the offering of] bulls with our lips"), because they will offer the *Korban Pesach* in actual deed in the *Beis HaMikdash HaShlishi*.

The Rebbe turned to the Rav (the renowned Torah scholar, etc., Rabbi Y.Y. Piekarski) and said: "Presumably, you will find a halachic basis (*heter*) so that they will be able to offer the *Korban Pesach* even without the four days of inspection."

Afterward, he turned to the contractor (*R. M. HaKohen Rivkin*) and said: "And prepare yourselves to recite the threefold blessing, *Birchas Kohanim*, in the *Beis HaMikdash HaShlishi*, this Pesach."

He concluded: "Thank you very much, and a kosher and joyous Pesach."


## שיחת יום ועש"ק ערב פסח ה'תנש"א

## 109

### Sicha of Erev Shabbos, Erev Pesach, 5751

**— After Mincha —**

1. The unique quality of the festival of Pesach in this year’s calendar (in addition to the standard timing of Pesach on the 15th of Nissan) is that it falls on Shabbos.

Within the fact that it falls on Shabbos itself, there is an added elevation stemming from the blessing of the "Shabbos HaGadol" that precedes it. As is known, from Shabbos, "all the days are blessed"—all six days of the week, up to and including the following Shabbos, which is itself blessed by the preceding Shabbos. This is even more pronounced than with other days of the week, due to the common denominator that both are days of Shabbos. And if every Shabbos draws down a blessing for the Shabbos that follows, then on "Shabbos HaGadol," a great blessing is certainly drawn down for the Shabbos that follows it, upon which the festival of Pesach falls.

An additional elevation in this year’s calendar is that the festival of Pesach occurs during Parshas Shemini.

One must explain the content, as well as the connection and relevance, of these qualities of Pesach this year (its timing on Shabbos, the special blessing from Shabbos HaGadol, and Parshas Shemini), including and especially regarding Erev Pesach. Beyond being the eve of a Yom Tov—and among the Yamim Tovim, the "first of the festivals"—it is also, in this year, Erev Shabbos, an Erev Shabbos that is blessed by Shabbos HaGadol, and falls within Parshas Shemini, as will be explained.

2. Pesach that falls on Shabbos:

Shabbos (the seventh day of the creation of the world) is connected to and indicates the perfection of the world, as our Sages said: "What was the world lacking? Rest. Shabbos came, rest came." That is, after the completion of the creation of the world during the six days of Bereishis, the world was lacking rest, and on Shabbos, the world was completed.

Pesach (when they were redeemed from Mitzrayim) is connected to and indicates the level of Elokus that is above the world. For even the perfection of the world is still within the category of "Mitzrayim" (Egypt), from the word *meitzar* (constriction/boundary). True perfection lies in the redemption from the constriction and boundary of the world, in a manner of skipping (*Pesach* is named for the skipping and passing over) above the parameters of the world.

In this year’s calendar, where the festival of Pesach falls on Shabbos, these two qualities (Pesach and Shabbos) are joined together—the level that is above the world (Pesach) is drawn down and permeates even the parameters of the world (Shabbos). Or, in other words: it is not only that Yisroel are redeemed and leave Mitzrayim—meaning they ascend to a level above the world—but more than that, they elevate the world itself to a level above the parameters of the world.

3. Shabbos (on which Pesach falls) which is blessed by "Shabbos HaGadol":

The essence of "Shabbos HaGadol" ("greatness" in the matter of "Shabbos") is that in addition to the perfection of the world (the essence of Shabbos), a "greatness" that is above the world is drawn down and created within it. That is, the world itself is elevated to a level above the world, as emphasized by the "great miracle" of "He who struck Mitzrayim through their firstborn" (for which it is called "Shabbos HaGadol"). The miracle is not in a manner of overriding nature (above nature), but in a manner that permeates nature itself to change and transform it ("He who struck Mitzrayim through their firstborn").

It can be said that the content of the blessing drawn from "Shabbos HaGadol" to the festival of Pesach every year is that the level above the world (Pesach) should also be drawn down and revealed within the parameters of the world, in the manner and likeness of the "great miracle" of "Shabbos HaGadol." This matter is emphasized even more in a Pesach that falls on Shabbos—where the blessing that the festival of Pesach receives from "Shabbos HaGadol" is visibly apparent in the timing of the festival of Pesach on Shabbos, in which the connection of the level above the world with the world is emphasized.

4. Parshas Shemini:

"Shemini" (the eighth) indicates a level above the world. For the reality of the world (even the perfection of the world) is connected with the number seven—the seven days of Bereishis, which are the seven days of the cycle. The number eight is connected with a level above the world, and alludes to the matters of the Geulah—redemption from the measurement and limitation of the parameters of the world.

(It should be noted that the quality of "Shemini" is also emphasized in the festival of Pesach—in addition to the fact that both emphasize the skipping above the world—in that the eighth day of Pesach (in the Diaspora) is especially connected (more than the other days of Pesach) to the future Geulah to come through Moshiach Tzidkeinu. This is why we read the prophecy of the Geulah, "And a shoot shall come forth from the stem of Yishai, etc.," and eat the "Moshiach Seudah," as is known and famous, the custom accepted from the Baal Shem Tov.)

"Shemini" is also from the word *shuman* (fat), which "permeates throughout" (as is the ruling in Shulchan Aruch)—this alludes to the fact that the elevation of "Shemini" which is above the world is also in a manner of fat that permeates throughout, meaning that it is drawn down and permeates the parameters of the world.

There is an added quality in this year’s calendar, where we read "Vayehi Bayom HaShemini" eight times, at which point there is an added emphasis on the two aspects of "Shemini"—both in the quality of the level of Elokus that is above the world, since the matter of "Shemini" is repeated and doubled in elevation upon elevation eight times, and in the drawing down and revelation within the parameters of the world ("fat" that "permeates throughout"), since the matter of "Shemini" itself is in a manner of "fat," as is known the saying "Shemini shemonah sheminah" (that when one reads "Shemini" eight times, the entire year is *sheminah*).

5. The explanation of the matter of connecting the level of Elokus that is above the world with the world (the common denominator and shared point in the details of the aforementioned matters in this year’s calendar)—in the Avodah of man:

It is known that the Avodah of man is divided into two general modes: (a) The Avodah of Tzaddikim—ordered Avodah ("the daily offerings in their order") as the order was established in the creation of man in the manner of "that G-d made man upright." (b) The Avodah of Baalei Teshuvah—in a manner of addition ("the additional offerings according to their law") and skipping ("to leap like a bull") relative to the order of creation, through which they arrive at a level above the parameters of creation, as our Sages said, "In the place where Baalei Teshuvah stand, complete Tzaddikim cannot stand," and more than that, "they cannot even stand there."

Among the differences between them in the times of the year—Shabbos and Pesach: Shabbos (the perfection of the world) belongs (primarily) to the Avodah of Tzaddikim, and Pesach (skipping above the world) belongs (primarily) to the Avodah of Baalei Teshuvah in the way of skipping, as it is written, "The voice of my beloved, behold he comes, leaping over the mountains, skipping over the hills," a leap and a skip above the Seder Hishtalshelus, in the manner and likeness of the leap in the Avodah of Teshuvah.

From this it is understood that in this year’s calendar, where Pesach falls on Shabbos [which indicates that the leap above the world is drawn down and permeates the parameters of the world (as mentioned in section 2), and is also emphasized in the other details of this year’s calendar, both in the connection to Shabbos HaGadol and in Parshas Shemini (as mentioned in sections 3-4)]—the connection of the Avodah of Tzaddikim and the Avodah of Baalei Teshuvah together is emphasized.

The point of this is that in addition to the elevation and perfection of the Avodah of Tzaddikim, "And your people are all Tzaddikim," a perfection that is from the perspective of the parameters of creation, there is added to the Avodah also the perfection of the Avodah of Teshuvah that is above the parameters of creation, as emphasized in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who "comes to bring the Tzaddikim back in Teshuvah."

6. It can be said that this matter is also alluded to in the special Avodah of Erev Pesach:

The special Avodah on Erev Pesach is the offering of the Korban Pesach after midday and after the slaughtering of the daily afternoon Tamid. Something similar exists in this time, through the recitation of the "Seder Korban Pesach" after the Mincha prayer, which corresponds to the daily afternoon Tamid, as it is written, "And we will render the offering of our lips instead of bulls." Therefore, "A person who is G-d-fearing and trembles at the word of Hashem must read it at its time, so that his reading will ascend in the place of its offering."

In the "Seder Korban Pesach" there is a puzzling matter—that its conclusion and seal is in a matter that is (seemingly) the opposite of the perfection of the Korban Pesach: "And if the Pesach is found to be a *treifah*, it does not count for him until he brings another"?!

It can be said that the inner content of the "Seder Korban Pesach" is alluded to in its conclusion and seal ("Everything follows the conclusion") that "if the Pesach is found to be a *treifah*, it does not count for him until he brings another"—for the positive:

"Korban Pesach"—"The offering is called Pesach for the skipping and passing over... all its services are by way of skipping and leaping"—indicates the closeness to the Ribono shel Olam (Korban from the word *kiruv*—closeness, the totality of Avodah) in a manner of skipping and leaping. And "Seder Korban Pesach"—that the skipping and leaping (is not a one-time matter, but) becomes a fixed order in his Avodah, meaning that the constant Avodah is in a manner of skipping and leaping in elevation upon elevation.

The conclusion and seal (the completion, perfection, and total sum) of the "Seder Korban Pesach": "And if the Pesach is found to be a *treifah*, it does not count for him until he brings another"—that even when his Avodah is in a manner of skipping and leaping, he reaches the conclusion that "it does not count for him," meaning that in relation to his true standing and state ("for him"), this is not considered an ascent (skipping and leaping) relative to the order of Avodah in the usual way, "until he brings another"—a closeness to the Ribono shel Olam by way of skipping and leaping (Korban Pesach) in a completely different manner, "another" for the positive, which is not in the same category at all relative to his previous Avodah, a skipping and leaping even relative to the skipping and leaping of the Korban Pesach itself.

According to this, it is understood that in the "Seder Korban Pesach," the matter of "bringing the Tzaddikim back in Teshuvah" is emphasized—that even after the perfection of Avodah in the usual way (the Avodah of Tzaddikim), including even after a regular order of skipping and leaping has been made in the Avodah of the Tzaddikim, a more elevated perfection is required and consequently achieved through a skipping and leaping that is completely incomparable.

It should be added that in the offering of the Pesach on Erev Shabbos (as in this year’s calendar), it is emphasized more that the skipping and leaping that is above the world (Pesach) is drawn down and permeates the parameters of the world (Erev Shabbos, the perfection of the world).

7. And furthermore, and this is the main point—that the totality of the matter of the festival of Pesach (which begins with the offering of the Korban Pesach) does not remain in the world of thought or the world of speech that is above the world of action, but is drawn down and permeates the parameters of the world of Asiyah—in action in practice, through the fact that immediately and truly the true and complete Geulah takes place through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, at which time we will offer the Pesach in action in practice, literally.

This matter is emphasized in the conclusion and seal of the recitation of the "Seder Korban Pesach"—that even after the elevation of "And we will render the offering of our lips," "that his reading will ascend in the place of its offering," nevertheless, according to the value of the elevation and perfection of the offering of the Korban Pesach in action in practice, this is like "the Pesach (which is through the recitation of the Seder Korban Pesach) is found to be a *treifah*, it does not count for him until he brings another"—another Korban Pesach that is not in the same category at all—the offering of the Korban Pesach in action in practice.

It can be said that "brings another" also alludes to the Avodah through which one arrives at the offering of the Pesach in practice literally in the true and complete Geulah—the Avodah of Teshuvah (which brings the Geulah), whose essence is to transform "another" (*acher*—to the *sitra achra*) into "one" (*echad*—holiness), the transformation of the letter *Reish* into a *Dalet*, through the fact that in place of the connection of the two lines (the upper line with the right line), one adds the point of the *Yud*, which alludes to the point of Yiddishkeit within every single Yisroel.

And furthermore, and the main point—that one does not suffice with the two lines in the letter *Dalet* (of "*Echad*"), which allude to thought and speech, meaning, as the Pesach is in thought and speech that are above the world of action, but "the action is the main thing," the offering of the Pesach in action in practice.

This matter is accomplished through the addition of a third line that is separated from the two lines (through which the *Dalet* becomes a *Heh*), which alludes to the action that is in a state of separation from speech and thought, to indicate the distance in value relative to speech and thought—a distance in value and separation for the positive (for the ultimate intent of thought and speech is for the sake of the action, which is the main thing), as alluded to in the verse "I have created it, I have formed it, I have also made it," the three worlds of BYA that correspond to thought, speech, and action, where the separation of "also (I have made it)" adds and increases a more elevated category that is incomparable—as alluded to also in the letter *Heh* (which is made through the addition of the third line), the fifth level, "a fifth for Pharaoh," "from which all the lights are revealed and shine," which is drawn down and revealed and permeates this world that was created with the letter *Heh*—the *Heh* of the *Yud-Heh* in the name Havayah, and even to the letter *Heh* as it is by itself—the fifth category (*Heh*), which is above the four letters of the name Havayah.

Its essence in the Avodah of man—that the order of Avodah is that there must be a separation between thought and speech and the action in practice, in order to return and contemplate once again how to perform the action in practice with the ultimate perfection and with an addition relative to thought and speech. And similarly in the conduct of the Ribono shel Olam (so to speak)—that even after the thought and speech regarding the Geulah, He returns and contemplates once again so that the Geulah in action in practice will be with the ultimate perfection and with an addition.

And especially through the addition in Tzedakah now (in addition to the effort in giving Tzedakah during the thirty days before Pesach)—"Great is Tzedakah, for it brings the Geulah near," that immediately and truly the true and complete Geulah comes through Moshiach Tzidkeinu in action in practice literally, below ten *tefachim*, as it is written, "And you shall be gathered one by one, O children of Yisroel," "with our youth and our elders, etc., with our sons and our daughters," and "their silver and their gold with them," and they come "with the clouds of heaven" to our holy land, to Yerushalayim the holy city, and to the third Beis HaMikdash, "The sanctuary, O Hashem, which Your hands have established," "and we will eat there from the sacrifices and from the Pesach offerings."

[The Rebbe gave each person a dollar bill to give (or exchange) for Tzedakah. And afterwards he said:]

8. We will conclude with a blessing—the blessing of a kosher and happy festival of Pesach, including also its being the "first of the festivals," which alludes to the pilgrimage to the third Beis HaMikdash, "The sanctuary, O Hashem, which Your hands have established."

And from blessing to blessing—to thank all those who expressed their wishes and good blessings (blessing from the word *himshech*—drawing down), and the matter has already been stated—whoever blesses is blessed, and with the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam, whose addition is greater than the main thing.

And in continuation of this—this is the place to also acknowledge the receipt of the letters of requests for blessings, *pidyonos*, etc., which were brought, etc., to the Ohel of the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation.

And may it be the will that there should be good news always all the days,

And it begins with the matter that the time causes—the completion of the preparations for Pesach, including and especially the recitation of the "Seder Korban Pesach,"

And all the more so in the matters of Pesach itself, the recitation of the Haggadah, and especially the "three things... Pesach, Matzah, and Maror"—in the third Beis HaMikdash that will be built speedily in our days, immediately and truly.


## שיחת יום ב', כ"ח ניסן ה'תש"נ

## 118

### Sicha of Monday, 28 Nissan, 5750

**— After Mincha —**

a. "We begin with a blessing".
Especially when we find ourselves in a time of auspiciousness—during the days of the month of Nissan, which is so named because "in it miracles were performed for Israel". It is a time of "miracles of miracles," as hinted at by the two *nuns* in the word *Nissan* (ניסן). As we have been mentioning and emphasizing throughout this month of Nissan of this year—the year 5750, which possesses the elevation of the fiftieth year—its acronym (as publicized throughout the Jewish world) is "It shall be a year of miracles." And in Nissan—more than three weeks have passed, following the elevation of the moon "standing in its fullness" on the fifteenth day of Nissan, and after all the days of Pesach (including Acharon Shel Pesach), and the Shabbos that followed, Shabbos Parshas *Vayehi B'yom HaShmini*, along with all the good "signs" contained in all of the above.

At such a time, the blessing of Hashem to every single Jew and to all of Bnei Yisrael is emphasized to the greatest degree, according to the measure of Hashem—"from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand". It is a blessing that has no limitation whatsoever. Together with this, it is drawn down in a way that Bnei Yisrael have the "capacity" to receive the blessing, and through this, there is an even greater addition in the drawing down of Hashem’s blessings, and in the capacity of Bnei Yisrael to receive the additional blessings.

And first and foremost—the blessing regarding the most essential and necessary matter: the miracle of the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, "I await him every day that he may come", in such a way that "He did not delay them even for the blink of an eye".

## 120

Men, women, and children should offer praise and thanksgiving to Hashem for all the goodness, blessings, and successes He has granted them, and will grant, and will grant again.

e. Furthermore, one must arouse [the people] regarding an increase in *tzedakah*—with this preface:
Although, in accordance with the instruction mentioned earlier to "think good," there is no place for the matter of fasting—it is understood that the negation of fasting due to the instruction to "think good" does not, Heaven forbid, detract from the elevation of giving *tzedakah* (in place of the fast), both in the quantity of the *tzedakah* and in the quality of the *tzedakah*.

Therefore, it is worthwhile and proper that in connection with the above, they should also increase in the giving of *tzedakah* in an amount equivalent to the cost of the meals for the day (in place of a fast)—an amount equivalent to two meals, and how much better an amount equivalent to three meals, as is the common custom of most Bnei Yisrael in these days. And all the more so regarding the giving of *tzedakah*, which, according to the ruling of the Rambam that "anything that is for the sake of the Good G-d should be of the finest and best... and so it says 'all the fat is for Hashem, etc.'," certainly one should add and give to *tzedakah* an amount equivalent to three meals, at whatever time each person chooses.

And it is best that the increase in *tzedakah* be connected also with a matter of Torah: to give *tzedakah* for the support of those who study Torah, or for institutions that engage in the dissemination of Torah study in every possible place.

f. You should certainly publicize the above matters in all the places where Bnei Yisrael reside, and to every one of them—men, women, and children.

And with emphasis—be careful not to cause fear, Heaven forbid, but rather to arouse [them] regarding the increase in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, out of expansiveness, true confidence, and out of joy and a good heart.

The main point is to increase in Torah, *tefillah*, and *tzedakah*. Regarding the details—as per the suggestion above, including that each person should assess and decide for themselves to increase even more in this direction and in this spirit.

g. And may it be His will—and this is the main thing—that the speech and the good resolutions regarding the above will hasten, expedite, and bring forward even more the fulfillment of the promise "Think good and it will be good" in actual reality, beginning with the true and essential good—the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

And especially through the increase in *tzedakah* now—as is customary in such instances, to give all those present here a *shlichus-mitzvah* for *tzedakah*, and they will surely add from their own—"Great is *tzedakah*, for it brings the Redemption closer", the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, immediately, now, in reality.

[The Rebbe Shlita gave each of those present two dollar bills—a *shlichus-mitzvah* to give to *tzedakah*.]


## משיחות ש"פ בהר, ט"ו אייר ול"ג בעומר ה'תשמ"ו

## 121

### From the sichos of Shabbos Parshas Behar, 15 Iyar and Lag B’Omer, 5746

12. It is a custom of Israel (which is Torah) from ancient times that on Lag B’Omer—the yom hilula of Rashbi and his day of rejoicing—one occupies oneself specifically with Jewish children, boys and girls. One takes them out into the field, or on a parade, or holds a gathering for them, and the like, in honor of the day of Rashbi’s rejoicing.

Therefore, it is appropriate to arouse—and "one only urges the eager"—that in every single place, one should add even more in making all the suitable preparations to gather as many children as possible on Lag B’Omer, for a parade or a gathering, in every location—in a manner appropriate to that place—so that it should be "in the multitude of people is the King’s glory".

And one should speak with them about the essence and manner of conduct of Rashbi and of Lag B’Omer in general, and what they must learn from this to strengthen their Torah study and performance of mitzvos.

And in order to add even more to this, it is a correct thing that, in addition to the teachers (male and female) and counselors (male and female) arousing the children to participate in the gatherings and the like, every child who already knows about Lag B’Omer and about a gathering or the like that will take place for children—should speak to and arouse at least one more child (a boy to another boy, and a girl to another girl) to participate in a gathering or the like in honor of Rashbi’s rejoicing.

This will add even more to the success and to the "multitude of people is the King’s glory," as one sees in practice, that when a child arouses his friend (or a girl, her friend), they can accomplish more than when adults do it, even the teachers themselves.

13. In this regard, it is worth adding that if in any place one cannot organize a gathering or a parade of children on Lag B’Omer, or one cannot do it completely—and in truth, even if one does it completely, one can always add to it, for there is no limit to goodness and holiness—one should, in the days following that come in the continuation of Lag B’Omer, hold (another) gathering, party, or parade and the like, for Jewish children, boys and girls, as a continuation of the day of Rashbi’s rejoicing on Lag B’Omer.

It is understood that one should speak there about the parsha of the day and the week (when the gathering takes place), but together with this, one should also connect it to Lag B’Omer and to Rashbi, as it is a gathering that comes as a continuation of Lag B’Omer.

It goes without saying that one should hold the gathering and the like in a manner that is permitted *lechatchila* (without any doubts in the matter) during the days of Sefira—by connecting it with a *seudas mitzvah*—a "siyum" on a tractate or the like, for "one makes a celebration for the completion of Torah", or with another *seudas mitzvah*, of which one will certainly find many opportunities.

And as mentioned, even in places where one has already held a gathering on Lag B’Omer itself, there is no limit to holiness—so one must certainly add to it by holding another gathering in these days.

Especially since we find ourselves in the *ikvesa d’meshicha* era, and at that very point—in the *ikvesa d’ikvesa*, moments before the Geulah—when there is the deepest, double and redoubled darkness, as per the parable of our Rebbes, that at the end of the night, before it becomes light at the break of dawn, is the deepest darkness (especially if one does not feel that this is a deep darkness). And one needs no proof for this, etc.

The intention in this is certainly that it should arouse Jews that they must add even more in light and holiness, in strengthening Torah study and the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur*, and through this—bring about that in this double and redoubled darkness, the rays of the break of dawn should already shine, of the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

This is accomplished specifically through the addition in light and holiness and strengthening of Torah and mitzvos by the *tinokos shel beis raban*—for "the world exists only for the sake of the breath of the *tinokos shel beis raban*," "breath that has no sin", and of them it is said, "Do not touch My anointed ones", and "From the mouths of babes and sucklings You have founded strength... to silence the enemy and the avenger".

Especially when one gathers them in a gathering in connection with the rejoicing of Rashbi—who "is worthy for one to rely upon in times of distress", which also applies to the distress and darkness of the Galus, and Rashbi said, "I can exempt the entire world from judgment, etc."—and the children rejoice in the rejoicing of Rashbi, a rejoicing of "breath that has no sin," a pure and holy rejoicing, etc., as one sees tangibly that the joy, *nigunim*, and dancing of children is with a simplicity, innocence, and liveliness and *shturem* more than with adults.

And this joy (in the rejoicing of Rashbi) comes together and adds to the good resolutions of the children to further solidify and strengthen their connection with Rashbi and with his ways of conduct, and simply—that the joy of the children in the rejoicing of Rashbi becomes an ongoing action for all times, to add in Torah study and in the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur*, permeated with *ahavas Yisrael* and *achdus Yisrael*, and to bring this into their homes and among their families and friends, etc.

And "Train a child according to his way, even when he grows old he will not depart from it", that they should grow up to be *lomdei Torah* and *mekaymei mitzvos* with *hiddur*, permeated with *yiras shamayim*, and especially—the study of the Torah of Rashbi, *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, and to be "candles to illuminate," to influence and illuminate their entire surroundings.

14. Regarding a related matter:
Lag B’Omer (the *Matan Torah* of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*) is also a preparation—within all the days of Sefira—for the time of the giving of our Torah on the festival of Shavuos, when there were "our children who guarantee us", the Jewish children were the "guarantors" for the giving of the Torah and the acceptance of the Torah until the end of all generations.

Therefore, it is a correct thing (as discussed in previous years) that on the day of the festival of Shavuos, during the reading of the Ten Commandments (which is in the likeness of the day of the giving of the Torah), one should bring all Jewish children, both boys and girls (also very small children), into the *beis knesses*—a "mikdash me'at"—in order to hear the Ten Commandments and the verses as a preface to this (at the very least).

15. In continuation of this (the matter of *chinuch*), in many places it is now also a *zman grama*, standing there close to the end of the school year for children, to influence the parents of Jewish children that they should send their children to a summer camp which is founded on *taharas hakodesh*, permeated with *ahavas Hashem* and *yiras Hashem*. And as discussed many times, one sees in practice that the effect of a summer camp on children (especially a summer camp for the entire day and night) is much stronger (in many details) than the effect of even a school—therefore it is even more relevant to pay attention that one should send the children to a summer camp that is appropriate for a Jewish child.

And it is also relevant that one should endeavor and influence the parents regarding the school year of the coming year—which now (close to the end of the school year of this year) the parents are beginning to think about—that the parents who sent their children to a "public school" should decide to send them in the coming year to a *cheder* or a *yeshiva* and the like.

16. May it be the will that through the very decision in the matter now—regarding gathering children both on Lag B’Omer (*Matan Torah* of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*) and on the festival of Shavuos (*Matan Torah* of *Nigleh D’Torah* and of the totality of Torah)—one should already immediately receive the reward, and in the language of the blessing every day (in the morning blessings), "Giver of the Torah," in the present tense—the acceptance of the Torah (*Pnimiyus HaTorah* and *Nigleh D’Torah*) in a new manner with a new vitality, etc.

And in addition, one also receives the reward that the time brings about, that the *zechus* and the powers of Rashbi should be drawn down here below and continue blessing for each and every one in all matters immediately in the time of Galus, as the words of Chazal that "Rashbi is worthy to rely upon in times of distress," which includes also the distress and darkness of the Galus (as above), which is a "time of distress" not only for Jews below, but "in all their distress, He is distressed", also a "time of distress" *kivayachol* above, until as Rashbi says, that "Israel is beloved before the Holy One, Blessed be He, that in every place they were exiled, the *Shechinah* is with them, etc."

Until the main reward—the true and complete Geulah—as a continuation of the statement of Rashbi: "And even when they are destined to be redeemed, the *Shechinah* is with them, as it is said, 'And Hashem your G-d will return [with] your captivity', and it does not say 'He will return' [transitive], but 'He will return' [intransitive], teaching that the Holy One, Blessed be He, returns with them from between the exiles."

And simply—that all Jews, "with our youth and with our elders... with our sons and with our daughters", go to greet the face of Moshiach Tzidkeinu—similar to "Who is the face of the Master? This is Rashbi"—in the manner of "And behold, with the clouds of heaven".

And one goes in the manner of "And I will lead you upright" (as one reads in the *Mincha* prayer of this Shabbos), and especially through the fact that one adds even more in "If you walk in My statutes", "that you shall be toiling in Torah", until similar to the "his Torah is his craft" of Rashbi, "And you shall keep My mitzvos and perform them", "Be toiling in Torah in order to keep and perform", and in a manner of "increasing and going on" in light.


## בס"ד. שיחת ל"ג בעומר בעת ה"פּאַראַד", ה'תשמ"ג

## 133

...a student of Rabbi Akiva. For he studied Torah, which is "entirely according to Rabbi Akiva"—the entire Oral Torah and the commentaries on the Written Torah are founded upon the teachings that Rabbi Akiva studied with his students in his time, and they subsequently transmitted it to their students until it reached us.

It follows that every Jew who studies Torah is a student of Rabbi Akiva. Consequently, when one comes into contact with another Jew—a child or anyone else—one must immediately remember that he is a student of Rabbi Akiva, and it is possible that he is a greater, better student than oneself.

And being a student of Rabbi Akiva, he is also a colleague of Rashbi (since Rashbi is a student of Rabbi Akiva).

Furthermore, every person, every creature, is a creature of the Ribono shel Olam; within him is the "Artisan who fashioned me," the Ribono shel Olam who created him.

Therefore, the fact that one has had the privilege of helping another by fulfilling "Love your fellow as yourself" in speech and also in action—this not only does not give him the right, Heaven forbid, to not treat the other with respect, but on the contrary: it places upon him an obligation to be even more careful in showing respect to the other. And to do so with joy, with great joy and a good heart.

And since every Jew is (as mentioned above) a student of Rabbi Akiva, a colleague of Rashbi, and a creature of the Ribono shel Olam—this demands, and provides the strength, to be able to carry out to the fullest extent the practice of treating every child, every Jew, and every person with respect, and certainly—not to harm the other in any way whatsoever, not in action, and not even in speech.

12. There is a wondrous Midrash that establishes and makes it even more understandable how a child young in years, or a child young in the knowledge of the matters of Yiddishkeit, has the strength to restrain himself and not infringe upon the honor of another, and certainly not to encroach upon the boundaries of another and take something from another, and on the contrary—to give, to show the other respect:

It is written, "Elokim stands in the congregation of El; in the midst of Elokim He judges." The Ribono shel Olam says that "Elokim stands"—He is present and stands with full strength—"in the congregation of El," where there is an *eidah* (a gathering) of people who are connected with *El*, with the Ribono shel Olam, with G-dliness.

The Midrash relates how this came to be. This was first...

## 135

And since the Ribono shel Olam stands with strength, "natzav" (stands), over the children—that strength is transferred, *kiviyachol*, to the children, so that they are *batel* and do not consider the *yetzer* at all.

The *yetzer* wants to convince him that the candy is tasty and the toy is beautiful, and he shouldn't care that another child was the first to want it, and certainly—the *yetzer* tells him—he doesn't need to rush to show respect to the other child.

However, because the child has received strength from "Elokim stands in the congregation of El," he is completely *batel* to the *yetzer*; the *yetzer* has no standing with him. He walks with "Elokim (who is) standing in the congregation of El," with the strength of the Ribono shel Olam, being *meshamesh* (serving) his Creator.

And then it is certain that the *yetzer* becomes completely *batel*, and the child is protected both in "turn away from evil" and in "do good," including also in treating one another with respect, that one shows respect to the other.

13. And then "we are all as one" is also realized; all Jews are united together as one thing. And then "Bless us, our Father" is realized, that the Ribono shel Olam blesses us with all blessings.

Until—with the main blessing and the essential blessing—that speedily in our days, literally, very soon "now," the Ribono shel Olam takes out every child and all children, together with their brothers, sisters, parents, grandmothers, and grandfathers, "with our youth and with our elders... with our sons and with our daughters", from *galus*.

And we all go together, as a "great congregation", a great "congregation of El," the wholeness of the people, the entire Jewish nation in its entirety, in body, in soul, and in property, taking with us the wholeness of Torah and *mitzvos*, everything that one has received through studying Torah, and in particular—from "his Torah is his craft" and through fulfilling *mitzvos* with joy and a good heart, until it becomes the wholeness of Torah and *mitzvos*.

And we go "with the clouds of heaven", "I will hasten it"—the Ribono shel Olam brings the Jews through clouds and in a very swift manner, in the language of the Rambam, "immediately they are redeemed"—into the true and complete *Geulah*, in our holy land, "a land which... the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year", and the Ribono shel Olam called it the King's palace; this is His palace.

And Torah has guaranteed that the land belongs as an eternal inheritance, as an everlasting heritage, to the eternal people, which was given to them...

## 136

...by the Eternal G-d, by the eternal Ribono shel Olam. It belongs to them—certainly the parts that Hashem has already given to the Jews, and certainly that one will not give back even a hairsbreadth of Hashem's gift.

And since one is also fulfilling the *mitzvah* of holding onto Hashem's gift, all the territories that have already been occupied in *Eretz HaKodesh*, which the Ribono shel Olam gave with miracles and with a welcoming countenance—this will further hasten that the Ribono shel Olam, through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, and in ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, will grant the land in its wholeness—the wholeness of the land to the Jews. The entire land in its wholeness is given to every Jew and to all Jews, in ways of peace, because this is given by the Ribono shel Olam, whose name is Peace.

Thus, all three wholenesses come together—the wholeness of the people, the wholeness of the Torah, and the wholeness of the land.

And it becomes, as Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai said, "How beloved are Yisrael before the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, that wherever they were exiled, the *Shechinah* is with them... They were exiled to Edom, the *Shechinah* is with them... And even when they are destined to be redeemed, the *Shechinah* is with them, as it is said, 'And Hashem your G-d will return with your captivity'—it does not say 'He will return [them],' but 'He will return [with them],' teaching that the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* returns with them from between the exiles."

Rashbi says that as long as even one single Jew, even a tiny little child, is still in *galus*, the *Shechinah* is still in *galus*. When the Ribono shel Olam takes all Jews out of *galus* through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, "And you shall be gathered one by one, O children of Yisrael", every Jew and all Jews, down to the last little child who is in *galus*—then the Ribono shel Olam also comes out of *galus*.

"And He will have mercy on you"—this all takes place with mercy, and through the fact that a Jew conducts himself with mercy toward another Jew (which "He will have mercy on you" also implies).

"Immediately they are redeemed" (as mentioned above). It is self-understood that when the Ribono shel Olam comes out of *galus*, He does not need, Heaven forbid, to rely on "trains" and "planes" and similar things, but "immediately they are redeemed," in one moment and "in the blink of an eye" (as it was in "the days of your coming out of the land of Egypt").

In the blink of an eye, one finds oneself standing in *Eretz HaKodesh*, and there itself in Jerusalem, the holy city, and there itself on the *Har HaBayis*, in the "Sanctuary, O Hashem, which Your hands have established", at the "front" by the gate and entrance of the *Beis HaMikdash HaShlishi*, which will be built speedily in our days, and "restore our service of the *Beis HaMikdash* to its place speedily in our days, *amen selah*".

***

## 137

14. We will likely conclude as we always conclude these gatherings (of children)—with the matter of a prayer, the prayer of "May it be Your will... that the *Beis HaMikdash* be built..."

This will come in addition to the many words of the Written and Oral Torah, the verses and sayings of *Chazal*, which were said and studied earlier.

And we will also give every child money so that he should give it (a portion of it) away on this very day of Lag B'Omer for *tzedakah*.

Then there will be the three pillars of Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*, which sustain the world so that it should not shake or tremble.

This is also the mission of the Jews: to bring peace into the world as well, through the fact that they bring peace among themselves, between one Jew and another (as discussed earlier), until a true peace, which then brings true peace into the world.

And certainly this will bring strength to the "small world," which is man, that in every Jew who engages in Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*, his "small world" will stand with the greatest strength.

15. Especially as we are in the days of *Sefirah*. This further emphasizes the strength and vitality with which Jews fulfill Torah and *mitzvos* (all three pillars of Torah, *avodah*, and *gemilus chasadim*):

One of the aspects of *Sefiras HaOmer* is that when they went out of Egypt, they already knew then that they were going toward *Matan Torah*, as they were told, "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve G-d on this mountain"—Jews counted the days toward *Matan Torah* with great longing, how many days had already passed from the Exodus until *Matan Torah*.

This is what Jews do every year, just as in this year—that immediately after the festival of Pesach, one begins to prepare for the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. One knows that forty-nine days must pass between them, so one counts the days with a longing for *Matan Torah*, how many days have already passed.

And standing on Lag B'Omer, one knows that thirty-three days have passed until today, so one must wait until...

## 140

...its nature is joy), and regarding saying "Naichem" (the prayer of consolation), joy is relevant, not *oneg* (delight). So it is understandable that he was permitted to say it and did say it on *Chol HaMoed*, which is a day of joy by Torah law; he was permitted to say it on Shabbos, which is not a day of joy (but of *oneg*).

However, the fact that he did not actually say it on Shabbos is not because of the holiness of Shabbos or *oneg Shabbos*, and that *oneg* is greater than joy, etc., because *oneg* has no connection with the recitation of "Naichem"—but rather because he had nowhere to say it, since the blessing of "Tishkon" is not recited then.

It turns out, according to the simple meaning of the language, that on every day, even on a day of joy by Torah law, *Chol HaMoed*, Rabbi Avraham HaLevi was permitted to say and did say "Naichem," because of his deep feeling regarding the *galus*.

Nevertheless, when the day of Lag B'Omer arrived, Rashbi says that he was not permitted to say "Naichem" then, because of the joy of that day, which is such a great joy that it outweighs even the sorrow that Rabbi Avraham HaLevi had from the destruction!

This further underscores the great joy of Rashbi on Lag B'Omer, that (there is a matter in this which) is even stronger than the joy of *Chol HaMoed*, which is "festivals for joy" by Torah law (the same "festivals for joy" as on the days of *Yom Tov* where work is forbidden), and even stronger than the joy of *Yom Tov* and Shabbos. The proof is that were it not for the aforementioned, he would have said "Naichem" on *Yom Tov* and Shabbos as well.

This is also the case regarding the joy of the future *Geulah*, that it is even greater than the joy of "festivals for joy,"

As it is stated in the Midrash that in the time to come "all festivals will be nullified, but the days of Purim will never be nullified." And there is an explanation for this: Heaven forbid to say that a *mitzvah* of the Torah will be nullified. Even then, one will also observe the festivals of Pesach, Shavuos, and Sukkos, but the joy of the *Geulah* and the days of Mashiach will be so great that "what use is a candle in the daylight?"—the joy of the festivals will not occupy a large place relative to the joy of the *Geulah*. This is not the case with the joy of Purim, which is "until one does not know." And similarly, one may say by way of possibility regarding the joy of Lag B'Omer (which is greater than the joy of "festivals for joy").

17. May the Ribono shel Olam help that from this taking part according to our strength in the great joy of Rashbi, through the fact that on this day...


## ויקרא

## 145

### Vayikra

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you have secured a position as a shochet of poultry in London: May it be His will that it be successful in every detail.

You also ask my opinion as to whether it is worthwhile to change your position to become a shomer for a shochet of cattle. In my opinion, it is not advisable. It is better that, at least for the initial period, you remain in the position of poultry shechitah. You should certainly endeavor to ensure that they are satisfied with your work.

It is appropriate that you assist, as much as your time working as a shochet allows, in the various branches of his work, and in the field most suited to your talents and abilities. The promise of the Alter Rebbe is well known: that in the merit of his mesiras nefesh, when Chassidim act in his matters, they will succeed.

It is surely unnecessary to urge you regarding the importance of setting fixed times for the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, especially when arriving in a new place, where the local people look at you as "one of the Lubavitcher Rebbe’s students," and as an example of what a Chassidishe shochet is.

(From a letter, 12 Teves 5712)

...I am writing to acknowledge receipt of your letter from 10 Shevat, along with the proposal for a new law regarding the matter of shechitah. Thank you for your attention to this.

Regarding the matter itself, and without entering into the details of the proposal: Since the manner of preparation for shechitah is also part of the matter of shechitah, just as there is no place for any government ministry to deliberate—and certainly not to legislate—anything concerning the laws of shechitah, so too there is no place for a government ministry to deliberate or legislate regarding the methods of preparation for shechitah, as this constitutes an infringement upon the freedom of religion in this country.

## 146

It is irrelevant here whether the intentions are well-meaning, or even if the text of the proposal contains no contradiction to the laws of the Shulchan Aruch. The fundamental principle here is that the government has no right or authority to interfere in the religious domain of any minority. Therefore, any discussion whatsoever on the part of an organization or government ministry in the field of religion is fundamentally flawed. It is not for the government to decide in cases where there are differences of opinion between rabbis regarding any religious matter.

(From a letter, 15 Shevat 5726)

Regarding your note on the matter of "placing on the ground" — it is proven from Menachos (7a and there) that even regarding Kodshim (and holiness), an object located inside a vessel is affected by the person holding the vessel placing it on the ground (though there are matters of holiness where this is not a disqualifying factor). See Shabbos 5b. Consequently, in matters of (holiness and) blessings and the like between one person and another (unlike the taking of the kemitzah or the sprinkling of blood), it is obvious that if one wishes for it to be a valid "giving," it is not nullified by being placed on the ground (Gittin 78a). The distinction regarding Kiddushin (8b) is understood.

(From a letter, Tammuz 5765)

## 147

...Regarding an asham that was lost, where one set aside another and then the first was found, and both are standing: It is not explicitly stated whether the law in this case is like the Korban Pesach, where one may sacrifice whichever he chooses (Rambam, Hilchos Korban Pesach, Chapter 4, Halacha 6), or like the bull and goat of Yom Kippur, where the first ones are sacrificed (Rambam, Hilchos Avodas Yom Kippur, Chapter 5, Halacha 16).

What appears to me in this matter is that where there is no explicit ruling, one should find support from elsewhere rather than innovating. Since the rule is stated—as is also brought in the sefer Erech Avod Pesach—that "anything that would be left to die in the case of a chatas is offered as an olah" (Nazir 25a) according to the version of Rabbeinu Tam, and "anything that would be left to die in the case of a chatas is offered as shelamim in the case of Pesach," the law is the same for both Pesach and asham. Even according to our version, where the asham is left to pasture, the halachic conclusion according to all opinions is that if one were to sacrifice it, he would not be liable for anything; it is only that the verse teaches us, etc.—meaning that the asham and olah are linked, and a verse is required, etc.

The logic that the asham and olah are two different sacrifices with different laws—well, in the case of Pesach and shelamim, the laws are also different, and yet one may sacrifice whichever he chooses...

(From a letter, 5720)


## ניסן

## 148

### Nissan

...Since we have entered the month of Nissan, in which we are destined to be redeemed, as the Midrash rules (Shemos Rabbah 15:11)—and the Midrash further states that this redemption is also an exodus from the "iron bondage" to the "bondage of Torah"—and based on what is written in Tanya, Chapter 37, that the matters of the days of Moshiach depend on our avodah throughout the time of golus, it is understood that now we must emerge from the "iron bondage" to the "bondage" (i.e., that which one does not easily initiate on one's own, but rather as a form of bondage and yoke, yet this bondage is the bondage) of Torah and mitzvos. Especially regarding the strengthening of institutions and Chabad activities in the field of chinuch al taharas hakodesh, in which Torah and mitzvos are combined—it is my hope that now you will add warmth, light, and vitality to the efforts for all of the above, and serve as a living example to other activists in this area within your surroundings, in addition to the efforts you make with them through speech. Our Sages of blessed memory have assured us, "You have labored and you have found," and the precision of the word "found" is well known—that it comes by way of a "finding," far exceeding what would be expected based on the labor alone.
(From a letter dated 4 Nissan, 5719)

It was with great sorrow and also astonishment that I read in your letter that you have abandoned your good and beautiful destiny—the chinuch al taharas hakodesh of the children of Yisrael, of whom it is said, "You are children to Hashem your G-d"—and exchanged it for, etc.

May it be the will of the Source of mercy and kindness that He pour out upon you a spirit from on high to recognize the truth, even though we live in an *alma d’shikra* (world of falsehood), for the Torah is eternal, in every place and at every time. The verse explicitly states, "The truth of Hashem is forever." As for the enticements of the *yetzer*, our Sages of blessed memory have said that a "spice" was created for it, and they said, "If this vile one encounters you, drag him to the beis medrash."

We are currently in days of *segulah*, the days of Nissan, in which, despite the situation of the children of Yisrael at that time, the people fled without calculations, arguments, or excuses. For if they had asked Pharaoh to let them go free, he would never have been forced to let them go, except, etc. (Tanya, Chapter 31, which concludes and seals: "This shall be my entire goal all the days of my life," etc. See there.)

In the above, the intention is simple, and is the hand of Hashem too short?

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,
(From a letter dated 3 Nissan, 5726)


## צו

## 149

### Tzav

It has been conveyed to me with pleasure regarding your gathering at a *seudas hodaah* (thanksgiving meal), that there are two primary themes in this: *Ahavas Yisrael*—"Love your fellow as yourself," which is a great principle of the Torah—and *hodaah* (gratitude) to Hashem, "for He is good, for His kindness endures forever," "Let them give thanks to Hashem for His kindness and His wonders to the children of men." This is the foundation of the renewal of the world, through which it is possible for the order of nature and the established systems of the world to be superseded by the performance of wonders for the children of men in this world.

May it be the will that, in accordance with the ruling and instruction of our Alter Rebbe—that *hodaah* serves as an indication and proof that one has completely returned to his source (Seder Birchas Hanehenin, Chapter 13, Law 5, based on the words of our Sages of old)—that through this *seudas hodaah*, you will draw down a complete recovery, until he returns to his full strength in every respect.

And may your reward be in the measure of the *Ribono shel Olam*, which is measure for measure, but many times over. In the manner of Hashem’s conduct in this: "I will not place upon you [from the outset]... for I am Hashem your healer," which is unlike the style of human medicine, as our Sages have stated regarding this.

With honor and blessing, that from here on out you shall only hear and share good tidings, in a revealed and manifest good, speedily and in our days.

(From a letter dated 2 Adar, 5719)


## פסח

## 150

### Pesach

In response to his question — regarding the custom among Jews that during the holiday of Pesach, a man and his household are together (and in his home) — and especially the head of the family. — In addition to the fact that it is extremely difficult to be *mehader* as one desires in matters of Pesach when one is in a different place. And the rest is understood.
[quotation](From a letter, 5726-7)[/quotation]

...Regarding his question about traveling here for a few weeks, while I do not see a necessity for this, since he writes that he has a source to cover the majority of the expenses, then why not? However, that the trip should be before Pesach and to celebrate the holiday of Pesach here, does not seem right to me, since the custom of Jewish men is to celebrate together with their household if at all possible. And since it was not essential until now, surely it does not matter if the trip is delayed by a few weeks...
[quotation](From a letter, 11 Shevat 5715)[/quotation]

I confirm receipt of your letter from Monday, in which you write about the highly important work of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, by learning with Jewish children and *Shabbos* gatherings. May *Hashem Yisbarach* help that it should be with great *hatzlacha* and in a manner of *mosif v'holech v'or* (increasing and going and shining). Especially since *chinuch* is a matter that yields fruits and the fruits of fruits, the importance of this is self-evident.
And this is also one of the hints of Pesach, to which we are now approaching,

## 151

when everything is about children, as it is written, "And you shall tell your son," etc., and as our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us, that *hem* (the children) *hikiru-hu* (recognized *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*) *techilah* (first) at the splitting of the sea.
With blessings for *hatzlacha* in all the above and for a *chag Pesach kasher v'sameach*.
[quotation](From a letter, 10 Nissan 5720)[/quotation]

B"H, 27 Nissan 5764
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the participants in the eleventh annual luncheon of *Agudas N'shei U'bnos Chabad* in Cleveland, Ohio
May *Hashem* sustain them
Blessing and peace:
With pleasure I received the news about your upcoming luncheon on Sunday, the first day of *Rosh Chodesh* Iyar (30 Nissan), may it come upon us for good.
May *Hashem Yisbarach* help that this annual undertaking should be crowned with great *hatzlacha* in all respects.
Since the undertaking takes place at the conclusion of the month of Nissan, it is to be hoped that on this occasion, the significance of this *Chodesh HaGeulah* and the holiday of Pesach will be emphasized for all Jewish women, and especially for Chabad women, and specifically regarding *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*. For the entire foundation of (the *Seder* and of) the *Haggadah* with which the holiday of Pesach begins is the *mitzvah* in the Torah, "And you shall tell your son" — to tell and explain to the children the significance of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, also as a preparation for *Kabbalas HaTorah*, in order to reach the level of "they recognized Him first" as it was at the splitting of the sea, with which the holiday of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* concludes.
The *Seder* and the *Haggadah* of Pesach teach us that one must not despair

## 152

even of a *ben rasha* (a wicked son), and one must bring him to the *Seder* table as well. At the same time, one must not rely on the *ben chacham* (wise son) that he will grow up to be a good and *frum* Jew on his own. One must occupy oneself with all Jewish children, without exception.
This is actually one of the tasks of Chabad women everywhere: to support the institutions and activities that aim to elevate all Jewish children to the level of a *ben chacham*. In addition to the primary task of *N'shei U'bnos Chabad* — to bring as much light and *kedushah* of *ner mitzvah v'torah ohr* into their homes and into their surroundings.
With blessings for *hatzlacha* and good tidings.

...I enjoyed what you wrote about the *farbrengen* of *Shabbos Mevarchim*, and especially that you also visited the homes of *Anash*. And surely the matter was done in a way that the women were also satisfied, and regarding what was discussed at the *farbrengen* of *Acharon Shel Pesach*, that the *geulah* of Pesach came about through the will of the women in this, and as explained in the *Midrash* that the righteous women influenced their husbands, and likewise at *Kabbalas HaTorah*, which is a continuation of the holiday of Pesach, and this continuation also includes the days in between. The verse specifies, "Thus shall you say to the house of Yaakov," etc., and our Sages, of blessed memory, explain in *Shemos Rabbah* that *Hashem* commanded to receive the consent of the women for this, and afterwards, etc...
[quotation](From a letter, 4 Iyar, 5715)[/quotation]

## 153

B"H, Tuesday *Parshas Vayikra el Moshe*,
*Rosh* *Chodesh* Nissan, 5750
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the sons and daughters of Yisrael
Wherever they may be
May *Hashem* sustain them
Peace and blessing!
As we stand on the day of *Rosh Chodesh* Nissan, the *Chodesh HaGeulah*, which *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* established as the first month of all the months of the year ("This month shall be for you the head of months; it is the first to you of the months of the year"), it is appropriate to reflect on the meaning and influence of the "Month of Redemption" in the daily life of a Jew throughout the entire year ("The head of months... of the year"), and especially for this year.
* * *
The beginning of the year is seemingly on the first day of the month of Tishrei — *Rosh Hashanah*. However, this is only according to the order of the creation of the world, as *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* created the world

## 154

and leads it "by way of nature," meaning in a way that from a superficial perspective, the leadership appears "natural," because *Elokus* is hidden and concealed within the garments of the nature of the world ("*Olam*" from the word *he'elem* [concealment], and similarly *Elokim* in *gematria* is "*hateva*" [nature]) — and every *Rosh Hashanah*, this natural divine leadership is renewed and strengthened.
And there is another divine leadership, "miraculous leadership," above nature, to the point that it breaks all the limitations of the nature of the world — and this leadership is connected with the month of Nissan (as is hinted in the name of the month — "*Nissan*" from the word *nes* [miracle]).
For this reason, too, this month is called by the name "Month of Redemption":
Simply, this is connected with *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, for by way of nature, as our Sages inform us, not even one single slave could have escaped from Mitzrayim, yet at *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, a great and mighty nation went out from there, with a high hand, more than six hundred thousand adult men (twenty years old and above), besides the young, and also women and children! But *Yetzias Mitzrayim* was through open miracles that *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* performed and showed, "He performed for our ancestors and for us all these miracles, He brought us out from slavery to freedom, etc." — and even before that, as a preparation for it — "Ten miracles were performed for our ancestors in Mitzrayim."
* * *

## 155

And more deeply: The connection of "miraculous leadership" to the "Month of Redemption" is not only in that the open miracles included (and the essence of them is) the departure from Mitzrayim simply, but also in that "miraculous leadership" is the internal content of "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*": "*Mitzrayim*" from the word *meitzarim u'gvulim* (limitations of nature), and "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*" means — a departure from all limitations. The innovation of miraculous divine leadership is — the revelation of *Elokus* in a manner completely above all the limitations ("*meitzarim u'gvulim*") of nature.
And just as this is regarding the entirety of Yisrael, so it is for each and every one of the children of Yisrael individually, that "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*" is the personal *geulah* from his own limitations of nature.
— This is the internal content of what is said, "When you bring the people out of Mitzrayim, you shall serve *Elokim* on this mountain": The perfection of "*ta'avdun*" (you shall serve) does not come only through the fulfillment of all the commandments of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, both in "turn from evil" and in "do good," and not only in absolute dedication to the service of *Hashem* with all one's strength and in all matters — but more than that: "With all your might," above the limitations of natural human powers. For this reason, it was in the ability of each one to reach "you shall serve *Elokim* on this mountain" only after "when you bring the people out of Mitzrayim," specifically the divine revelation of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* contains the power of above nature to elevate and raise each one above the limitations of nature and bring him to the perfection of "you shall serve *Elokim*," which is the "redemption of Mitzrayim," the personal *geulah* of each one individually.
* * *
It is understood that the revelation of *Elokus* in "miraculous leadership," being completely above the boundaries of nature, cannot be absorbed all at once and entirely by the intellect and powers of man, which, however elevated they may be, are nevertheless limited within the boundaries of nature. In other words: even when one sees with physical eyes open divine miracles, it is nevertheless not absorbed and grasped by the powers and senses in a penetrating and exhaustive way, and the matter remains beyond us.
We find this content explicitly in the Torah, and indeed in connection with the miracles of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, which at the end of the fortieth year of their being in the desert, Moshe Rabbeinu said to the children of Yisrael:

## 156

"You have seen all that *Hashem* did before your eyes in the land of Mitzrayim to Pharaoh and to all his servants and to all his land... But *Hashem* has not given you a heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear, until this day... forty years... And you came to this place... And you shall keep the words of this covenant and do them."
And this requires explanation: The verse itself emphasizes that the children of Yisrael saw with their eyes all the great wonders of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, and if so, how is it that they did not understand, did not see, and did not hear the miracles until the end of the forty years in the desert? — But here it speaks of such seeing, hearing, and recognition that will lead to "and you shall keep the words of this covenant and do them," a seeing, hearing, and recognition that encompasses and influences a person to keep the "words of the covenant" to the fullest extent (as Rashi says that "from here on, *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* will be strict" that it should be "and you shall keep the words of the covenant"),
to the point that the matter encompasses the person and penetrates him in all details — both in the heart (to know), both in the eyes (to see), and both in the ears (to hear), and this is also hinted at in that we find in the *Korban Pesach* (meaning even before they left Mitzrayim) that all parts of the *korban* are roasted together on the fire — "its head with its legs and its innards," and afterwards they eat the *korban*, at which time the *korban* becomes "blood and flesh like its flesh." Meaning — the full and perfect sacrifice to *Hashem* must encompass the entire person, and the eating of the *korban* must be during a continuous duration of one meal, "in one house," and for all the members of the house.
And for this, a one-time seeing, hearing, and recognition of the signs and wonders through simple senses was not enough, but rather a deep, internal, and prolonged soul-contemplation of the miraculous leadership of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* is required, so that the supernatural divine revelation will be soaked, filled, and thoroughly penetrated in all parts of the person's reality, until he transports himself and rises above all his limitations of nature. For this, a duration of forty years was required, to learn and delve into this, as our Sages learn from the aforementioned verse that "a person does not stand on the mind of his teacher until forty years" (— a person does not grasp the mind of his teacher until forty years).

## 157

This also gives a deeper explanation as to why Moshe Rabbeinu said these things to the children of Yisrael only after they stood to enter the land of Yisrael, on the threshold of a new period in the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* (in the land of Yisrael, the possibility was given to also fulfill the *mitzvos* dependent on the land, all the 613 *mitzvos*), this is because only at the end of the forty years in the desert, when the children of Yisrael merited a "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear" all the "great trials... the great signs and wonders" of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, were the conclusion and perfection of "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*" achieved, which lead to the keeping of the words of the covenant in a full and absolute manner.
* * *
The aforementioned matters have a special significance in this year:
We are "forty years" after the passing of the *Nasi* of our generation, *k"k mo"h Admur*, in whom one saw openly "miraculous leadership," supernatural, both in the physical sense and in the spiritual sense, one saw his supernatural *mesiras nefesh* in all areas of Torah and Yiddishkeit, as is well-known, and after forty years one reaches "stands on the mind of his teacher" — *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* gives a "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear," including and especially the miraculous leadership of the *Nasi* of our generation.
* * *

## 158

May it be the will that as we stand in the auspicious days of the month of Nissan in the year "*Hi Tihiyeh*" (It shall be), "a year of miracles," each one will merit to see tangibly in his own life the miraculous leadership of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* up to "miracles of miracles."
Up to the merit of the primary miracle — the miracle of the true and complete *geulah* by *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, in Nissan they were redeemed and in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed, at which time the miracles will be even greater in value and in a wonderful way than the miracles that were at *Yetzias Mitzrayim*. And as our Sages, of blessed memory, interpret: "As in the days of your departure from the land of Mitzrayim, I will show him wonders" — that even in relation to "the days of your departure from the land of Mitzrayim" they are "wonders."
And *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* fulfills the heartfelt prayer of every Jew and all Jews: "May my prayer come before You, incline Your ear to my cry" and brings the true and complete *geulah*,
and we enter immediately into the land of Yisrael — like the entry into the land of Yisrael the first time, which was immediately at the end of "forty years"
and all this — immediately and literally.
With respect and blessing for *hatzlacha* in all the above
And with the blessing of a *chag Pesach kasher v'sameach* and bearer of good news
Place of signature
[new_section]

## 159

B"H, Friday *Parshas Tzav*,
11 Nissan, *Nasi* for the sons of Asher, 5750
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the sons and daughters of Yisrael
Wherever they may be
May *Hashem* sustain them
Peace and blessing!
In continuation of the previous letter, from the day of *Rosh Chodesh* Nissan, and in order to clarify more the fundamental point that was explained in it — that the "conclusion" of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* and its perfection were at the end of the forty years in the desert, when the children of Yisrael merited a "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear" all the "great trials... the great signs and wonders" of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, in a way that all this was absorbed and penetrated well and filled all parts of the person: both the heart (to know), both the eyes (to see), and both the ears (to hear),
— it is appropriate to delve more and understand in a more fundamental way the innovation in the "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear" as they were after forty years in relation to the knowledge, seeing, and hearing that were at the time of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*,
and that the contemplation should be in a way that the matter will find expression up to action in practice,

## 160

and that it should be — like all matters of good and *kedushah* — in a manner of "we elevate in *kedushah*."
* * *
Just as we see in the physical life of a person that the heart conveys vitality ("for the blood is the soul") to all the limbs (as the saying goes: "*Liba palig l'chulei shiyfei*" — the heart distributes to all the limbs) — so it is in the spiritual vitality of a Jew, that in accordance with the depth and strength of the feeling of the Jewish heart toward *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, to that extent the matter is expressed in the service of *Hashem* in all the "limbs," the powers of his soul.
As is known, there are two general levels in the "service of the heart" — the yearning of the Jewish heart toward *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, which is the source and root of the service of *Hashem*:
One level is that a Jew is drawn and desires to draw closer and closer to *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* with the feeling of his heart, and a more elevated level — "the inwardness of the (Jewish) heart," which is a "movement" and feeling of complete connection and *dveikus* with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, the inwardness of the point of the heart that is completely connected and united with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, more than a person is dependent and united in his life, in his source of life.
And as stated — "*Liba palig l'chulei shiyfei*": In accordance with the two types of levels in the heart is the change in the action of the heart in all the powers and limbs of the person in the three general matters mentioned: (heart) to know, (eyes) to see, (ears) to hear — a change between the influence in the regular way and the influence in the elevated and deep way of knowledge, seeing, and hearing, because they stem from the *dveikus* of the inwardness of the heart and therefore they are in a more elevated way.
* * *
(Heart) to know: There is an understanding in *Elokus* according to the intellect of the limited man which is called by the name "*Da'as*

## 161

*Tachton*" (lower knowledge), as the "lower" strives (from below to above) to understand *Elokus* (as much as a created being can grasp the knowledge of the Creator);
And there is a mode of "*Da'as*" — "*Da'as Elyon*" (higher knowledge) — which is a completely different type of knowledge, as the "higher" understands *Elokus*, and this is the "to know *Hashem*" as He is connected — in the language of the *Rambam* — to the "hidden matters," the divine matters that are concealed, which cannot be grasped by regular human intellect and only from the side of the internal connection of the Jewish soul with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* (being a "part of *Elokah* from above, literally") is a Jew capable of reaching the more elevated understanding in *Elokus*;
(Eyes) to see: In seeing a thing, there is a huge difference between seeing it for the first time and contemplating it after a fundamental recognition of it and a contemplation of a long time in all its details, at which time it is a completely different "seeing."
The main difference is not that in one glance all the details of the thing are not absorbed and grasped — for as is known, the sense of sight has the quality to absorb and see the thing entirely in all its details, but rather that a seeing that comes after contemplation of the details of the thing is in a completely different fundamentalism and depth, it is a penetrating and deep contemplation that "grasps" the entire person, he is completely immersed and concentrated in the thing as if there is nothing else besides the thing he is seeing.
It is understood that then the thing is seen with all its details in a completely different light;
(Ears) to hear: There is "hearing" in general, and there is a soul-"hearing" which means deep and internal absorption, a "hearing" that penetrates and encompasses the entire essence of the listener — "Let my words enter your ears," and its influence is general and completely full until there is a hearing that touches

## 162

the entirety (and essence) of the person, and as the *halachic* ruling, "One who causes deafness must pay him the value of his entire body" (whoever caused deafness afterwards is obligated to pay him the value of his entire body).
* * *
This level of the inwardness of the heart is called by the name "*Eitan*," as *k"k Admur HaZaken* explains, and his words are:
